## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a population (dP_dt) as a function of time (t) and current population size (P), a classic ordinary differential equation setting in population ecology. The goal is to discover the mathematical law governing population growth, which often includes density-dependent feedback, carrying capacity, Allee effects, and possibly time-varying environments.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, constant per capita growth rate)
- Logistic growth (quadratic form): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (density-dependent regulation, c1 negative to create a stable equilibrium)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (asymmetric density dependence, often with slower approach to carrying capacity)
- Generalized logistic (thetaŌĆælogistic): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**(1 + c2) (flexible densityŌĆædependence exponent)
- Allee effect (cubic): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (negative growth at low density, positive at intermediate, negative near carrying capacity)
- Harvesting / constant mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 (constant removal leading to a lower or zero equilibrium)
- Exponential density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * P) (RickerŌĆætype growth, strong suppression at high densities)
- Linear timeŌĆævarying growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * t * P (environmental trend linearly affecting per capita growth)
- Resource depletion: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 + c2 * t) (carrying capacity declining over time due to resource consumption)
- Seasonal forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P * sin(c2 * t + c3) (periodic environmental variation, can produce cycles)
- Positive density dependence (Allee): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) (growth rate negative below threshold, positive above, no upper limit)
- DensityŌĆædependent mortality with decay: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 * exp(c2 * P) (stronger regulation at high densities)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- A linear term c0*P with c0>0 and no other PŌĆædependence suggests explosive exponential growth; a negative quadratic term c1*P**2 introduces a limiting carrying capacity (logistic).
- The presence of a cubic term P**3 in dP_dt, especially with alternating signs, indicates an Allee effect: two nonŌĆæzero equilibria, one unstable (threshold) and one stable.
- A term P*log(P) or P*log(c*P) points to Gompertz growth, which yields a sigmoid but asymmetric P(t) curve, often with slower lateŌĆæstage approach to the asymptote.
- If dP_dt contains explicit, nonŌĆædecaying time functions (e.g., sin, linear t, exp(t)), it implies a changing environment or resource depletion acting on the population growth rate.
- A constant negative term subtracted from growth (c0 * P ┬▒ ŌĆ” + c2 with c2<0) models constant harvesting or mortality; the longŌĆæterm population may stabilize lower or go extinct.
- Exponential dependence on P, such as dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * P), implies very strong densityŌĆædependent suppression, typical of overcompensatory dynamics (Ricker).
- A fractional power P**(1 + c2) in the growth equation (thetaŌĆælogistic) allows flexible asymmetry in the growth curve, accommodating various speciesŌĆæspecific densityŌĆædependence shapes.
- Multiplicative interaction between P and a decaying time term (e.g., P * (c1 + c2*t) with c2<0) signals a linearly declining carrying capacity due to resource depletion.
- Periodic modulation of the growth coefficient (P * sin(c2*t + c3)) introduces seasonal forcing; the model then predicts sustained population cycles rather than monotonic equilibration.
